<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Etymology 1"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm"><a href="/wiki/dogge#Middle_English" title="dogge">dogge</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> (akin to <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scots_language" class="extiw" title="w:Scots language">Scots</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="sco"><a href="/wiki/dug#Scots" title="dug">dug</a></i>), from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/dogga#Old_English" title="dogga">dogga</a></i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/docga#Old_English" title="docga">docga</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> of uncertain origin.
</p><p>The original meaning seems to have been a common dog, as opposed to a well-bred one, or something like '<a href="/wiki/cur" title="cur">cur</a>', and perhaps later came to be used for stocky dogs. Possibly a pet-form diminutive with suffix <i class="Latn mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/-ga#Old_English" title="-ga">-ga</a></i> (compare <i class="Latn mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/frocga#Old_English" title="frocga">frocga</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">frog</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/Reconstruction:Old_English/picga" title="Reconstruction:Old English/picga">*picga</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">pig</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>), appended to a base <i class="Latn mention" lang="ang"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconstruction:Old_English/dog-&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Reconstruction:Old English/dog- (page does not exist)">*dog-</a></i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="ang"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconstruction:Old_English/doc-&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Reconstruction:Old English/doc- (page does not exist)">*doc-</a></i> of unclear origin and meaning. One possibility is <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/dox#Old_English" title="dox">dox</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">dark, swarthy</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span> (compare <i class="Latn mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/frocga#Old_English" title="frocga">frocga</a></i> from <i class="Latn mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/frox#Old_English" title="frox">frox</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Another proposal is that it derives from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-West_Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-West Germanic language">Proto-West Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="gmw-pro"><a href="/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-West_Germanic/dugan" title="Reconstruction:Proto-West Germanic/dugan">*dugan</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to be suitable</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, the origin of <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/dugan#Old_English" title="dugan">dugan</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">to be good, worthy, useful</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/dow#English" title="dow">dow</a></i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de"><a href="/wiki/taugen#German" title="taugen">taugen</a></i>. The theory goes that it could have been an epithet for dogs, commonly used by children, meaning "good/useful animal.".<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Another is that it is related to <i class="Latn mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/Reconstruction:Old_English/docce" title="Reconstruction:Old English/docce">*docce</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">stock, muscle</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from Proto-West Germanic <i class="Latn mention" lang="gmw-pro"><a href="/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-West_Germanic/dokk%C4%81" title="Reconstruction:Proto-West Germanic/dokkā">*dokkā</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">round mass, ball, muscle, doll</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, whence English <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/dock#English" title="dock">dock</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">stumpy tail</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>. 
</p><p>In 14th-century England, <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/hound#English" title="hound">hound</a></i> (from Old English <i class="Latn mention" lang="ang"><a href="/wiki/hund#Old_English" title="hund">hund</a></i>) was the general word for all domestic canines, and <i>dog</i> referred to a subtype resembling the modern mastiff and bulldog.<sup id="cite_ref-dog_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dog-6">[6]</a></sup> By the 16th century, <i>dog</i> had become the general word, and <i>hound</i> had begun to refer only to breeds used for <a href="/wiki/hunt" title="hunt">hunting</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> In the 16th century, the word <i>dog</i> was adopted by several continental European languages as their word for <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/mastiff#English" title="mastiff">mastiff</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> 
</p><p>Despite similarities in forms and meaning, not related to <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mbabaram_language" class="extiw" title="w:Mbabaram language">Mbabaram</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="vmb"><a class="mw-selflink-fragment" href="#Mbabaram">dog</a></i>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Noun"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><span class="headword-line"><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">dog</strong> (<i><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#countable" title="Appendix:Glossary">countable</a> and <a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#uncountable" title="Appendix:Glossary">uncountable</a></i>, <i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/dogs#English" title="dogs">dogs</a></b>)</span>
</p>
<ol><li>A <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/mammal#English" title="mammal">mammal</a> of the <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/family#English" title="family">family</a> <span class="biota"><a href="/wiki/Canidae#Translingual" title="Canidae">Canidae</a></span>:
<ol><li>The <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/species#English" title="species">species</a> <span class="biota"><a href="/wiki/Canis_familiaris#Translingual" title="Canis familiaris"><i>Canis familiaris</i></a></span> (sometimes designated <span class="biota"><a href="/wiki/Canis_lupus_familiaris#Translingual" title="Canis lupus familiaris"><i>Canis lupus familiaris</i></a></span>), <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/domesticated#English" title="domesticated">domesticated</a> for thousands of <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/years#English" title="years">years</a> and of highly variable appearance because of <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/human#English" title="human">human</a> breeding.
<span class="HQToggle" style="margin-left: 5px;"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><span class="None" lang="und"><b>1918</b></span>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/W._B._Maxwell" class="extiw" title="w:W. B. Maxwell">W[illiam] B[abington] Maxwell</a>, chapter XVI, in <cite>The Mirror and the Lamp</cite>, Indianapolis, Ind.: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bobbs-Merrill_Company" class="extiw" title="w:Bobbs-Merrill Company">The Bobbs-Merrill Company</a>, <small><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.worldcat.org/title/4293071">→OCLC</a></small>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation cited-passage" lang="en">The preposterous altruism too!<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span>Resist not evil. It is an insane immolation of self—as bad intrinsically as fakirs stabbing themselves or anchorites warping their spines in caves scarcely large enough for a fair-sized <b>dog</b>.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><span class="None" lang="und"><b>1963</b></span>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Margery_Allingham" class="extiw" title="w:Margery Allingham">Margery Allingham</a>, chapter 19, in <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_China_Governess" class="extiw" title="w:The China Governess">The China Governess: A Mystery</a></cite>, London: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chatto_%26_Windus" class="extiw" title="w:Chatto &amp; Windus">Chatto &amp; Windus</a>, <small><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.worldcat.org/title/483591931">→OCLC</a></small>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation cited-passage" lang="en">When Timothy and Julia hurried up the staircase to the bedroom floor, where a considerable commotion was taking place, Tim took Barry Leach with him.<span class="q-hellip-sp">&nbsp;</span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>. The captive made no resistance and came not only quietly but in a series of eager little rushes like a timid <b>dog</b> on a choke chain.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul>
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">The <b>dog</b> barked all night long.</i></div></dd></dl></li>
<li>Any member of the family Canidae, including domestic dogs, wolves, coyotes, jackals, foxes, and their relatives <span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">extant and extinct</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span>; <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/canid#English" title="canid">canid</a>.
<span class="HQToggle" style="margin-left: 5px;"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><span class="None" lang="und"><b>1989</b></span>, John L. Gittleman, <cite>Carnivore Behavior, Ecology, and Evolution</cite>, page <span class="None" lang="und">561</span>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation cited-passage" lang="en">This includes the development of hyena-like bone crushers (<i>Osteoborus</i> and <i>Borophagus</i>), a large bone-crushing hunting <b>dog</b> (<i>Aelurodon</i>), and another borophagine frugivorous <b>dog</b> (<i>Carpocyon</i>).</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="usage-label-sense"><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">often <a href="/wiki/Appendix:English_nouns#Attributive" title="Appendix:English nouns">attributive</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span></span> A male dog, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/wolf#English" title="wolf">wolf</a><span class="serial-comma">,</span> or <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fox#English" title="fox">fox</a>, as opposed to a <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/bitch#English" title="bitch">bitch</a> or <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/vixen#English" title="vixen">vixen</a>.
<span class="HQToggle" style="margin-left: 5px;"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><span class="None" lang="und"><b>1908</b></span>, <cite>Dogdom</cite>, volume 9, page <span class="None" lang="und">337</span>, column 1:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation cited-passage" lang="en">Entirely disregarding sex, Ch. Searchlight has a beautiful Cocker head, but as he is a <i><b>dog</b></i>, his head is too fine and far too much upon the bitchy order.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><span class="None" lang="und"><b>1928</b></span>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siegfried_Sassoon" class="extiw" title="w:Siegfried Sassoon">Siegfried Sassoon</a>, <cite>Memoirs of a Fox-Hunting Man</cite>, Penguin, published <span class="None" lang="und">2013</span>, page <span class="None" lang="und">149</span>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation cited-passage" lang="en">Firstly, he was there to encourage and assist the hounds (a scratch pack – mostly <b>dog</b>-hounds drafted from fox-hound kennels because they were over-sized) <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span></span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol></li>
<li><span class="usage-label-sense"><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#uncountable" title="Appendix:Glossary">uncountable</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span></span> The <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/meat#English" title="meat">meat</a> of this animal, eaten as food.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">Did you know that they eat <b>dog</b> in South Korea?</i></div></dd></dl></li>
<li>A person:
<ol><li><span class="usage-label-sense"><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#slang" title="Appendix:Glossary">slang</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/derogatory#English" title="derogatory">derogatory</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span></span> A <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/dull#English" title="dull">dull</a>, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/unattractive#English" title="unattractive">unattractive</a> <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/girl#English" title="girl">girl</a> or <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/woman#English" title="woman">woman</a>.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">She’s a real <b>dog</b>.</i></div></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="usage-label-sense"><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#slang" title="Appendix:Glossary">slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span></span> A <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/man#English" title="man">man</a>, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/guy#English" title="guy">guy</a>, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/chap#English" title="chap">chap</a>.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">You lucky <b>dog</b>!</i></div></dd></dl></li>

<ol><li>Any of various mechanical devices for holding, gripping, or fastening something, particularly with a tooth-like projection.

<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Synonyms">Synonyms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Synonyms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<ul><li><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">animal</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span><span class="ib-colon sense-qualifier-colon">:</span> taxonomic names: <span class="biota"><a href="/wiki/Canis_familiaris#Translingual" title="Canis familiaris"><i>Canis familiaris</i></a></span>, <span class="biota"><a href="/wiki/Canis_domesticus#Translingual" title="Canis domesticus"><i>Canis domesticus</i></a></span>, <span class="biota"><a href="https://species.wikimedia.org/wiki/Canis_familiarus_domesticus" class="extiw" title="wikispecies:Canis familiarus domesticus"><i>Canis familiarus domesticus</i></a></span>, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canis_canis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Canis canis (page does not exist)">Canis canis</a></i>, <i>Canis aegyptius</i>, <i>Canis familiarus aegyptius</i>, <i>Canis melitaeus</i>, <i>Canis familiarus melitaeus</i>, <i>Canis molossus</i>, <i>Canis familiarus molossus</i>, <i>Canis saultor</i>, <i>Canis familiaris saultor</i></li>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Verb"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><span class="headword-line"><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">dog</strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en s-verb-form-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/dogs#English" title="dogs">dogs</a></b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en ing-form-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/dogging#English" title="dogging">dogging</a></b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en ed-form-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/dogged#English" title="dogged">dogged</a></b>)</span>
</p>
<ol><li><span class="usage-label-sense"><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#transitive" title="Appendix:Glossary">transitive</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span></span> To <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/pursue#English" title="pursue">pursue</a> with the <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/intent#English" title="intent">intent</a> to <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/catch#English" title="catch">catch</a>.
<span class="nyms-toggle" style="margin-left: 5px;"><a>synonyms&nbsp;▲</a></span><dl><dd><span class="nyms synonym"><span class="defdate">Synonyms:</span> <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/chase#English" title="chase">chase</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/chase_after#English" title="chase after">chase after</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/go_after#English" title="go after">go after</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/pursue#English" title="pursue">pursue</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/tag#English" title="tag">tag</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/tail#English" title="tail">tail</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/track#English" title="track">track</a></span>, <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/trail#English" title="trail">trail</a></span></span></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="usage-label-sense"><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#transitive" title="Appendix:Glossary">transitive</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span></span> To <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/follow#English" title="follow">follow</a> in an <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/annoying#English" title="annoying">annoying</a> or <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/harass#English" title="harass">harassing</a> way.
<span class="HQToggle" style="margin-left: 5px;"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;▼</a></span><dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">The woman cursed him so that trouble would <b>dog</b> his every step.</i></div></dd></dl>
<ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><span class="None" lang="und"><b>1749</b></span>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henry_Fielding" class="extiw" title="w:Henry Fielding">Henry Fielding</a>, <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_History_of_Tom_Jones,_a_Foundling" class="extiw" title="w:The History of Tom Jones, a Foundling">The History of Tom Jones, a Foundling</a></cite>, volumes <span class="maintenance-line" style="color: #777777;">(please specify |volume=I to VI)</span>, London: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrew_Millar" class="extiw" title="w:Andrew Millar">A<span style="font-style: normal;">[</span>ndrew<span style="font-style: normal;">]</span> Millar</a>,<span class="q-hellip-sp">&nbsp;</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">[</span></span><span title="over-against Catharine-street in the Strand">…</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>, <small><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.worldcat.org/title/928184292">→OCLC</a></small>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation cited-passage" lang="en"><span class="q-hellip-sp"></span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>…<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"> </span> they were discovered in a very improper manner by the husband of the gypsy, who, from jealousy it seems, had kept a watchful eye over his wife, and had <b>dogged</b> her to the place, where he found her in the arms of her gallant.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2012</b> January, Michael Riordan, “Tackling Infinity”, in <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Scientist" class="extiw" title="w:American Scientist">American Scientist</a></cite>‎<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20130430074403/http://www.americanscientist.org/bookshelf/pub/tackling-infinity">[6]</a></sup>, volume <span class="None" lang="und">100</span>, number 1, archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.americanscientist.org/bookshelf/pub/tackling-infinity">the original</a> on <span class="mw-formatted-date" title="2013-04-30">30 April 2013</span>, page <span class="None" lang="und">86</span>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation cited-passage" lang="en">Some of the most beautiful and thus appealing physical theories, including quantum electrodynamics and quantum gravity, have been <b>dogged</b> for decades by infinities that erupt when theorists try to prod their calculations into new domains. Getting rid of these nagging infinities has probably occupied far more effort than was spent in originating the theories.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2012</b> May 9, Jonathan Wilson, “Europa League: Radamel Falcao's Atlético Madrid rout Athletic Bilbao”, in <cite>the Guardian</cite>‎<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.guardian.co.uk/football/2012/may/09/atletico-madrid-athletic-bilbao-europa-league">[7]</a></sup>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation cited-passage" lang="en">But this is not an Athletic that ever looks comfortable at the back – a criticism that has often <b>dogged</b> Marcelo Bielsa's sides.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2021</b> June 21, Daisuke Wakabayashi, “Google Executives See Cracks in Their Company’s Success”, in <cite>The New York Times</cite>‎<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2021/06/21/technology/sundar-pichai-google.html">[8]</a></sup>, <small><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.worldcat.org/issn/0362-4331">→ISSN</a></small>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation cited-passage" lang="en">Yet Google, which was founded in 1998, is <b>dogged</b> by the perception that its best days are behind it.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="usage-label-sense"><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#transitive" title="Appendix:Glossary">transitive</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/nautical#English" title="nautical">nautical</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span></span> To fasten a <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/hatch#English" title="hatch">hatch</a> securely.
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="en">It is very important to <b>dog</b> down these hatches.</i></div></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="usage-label-sense"><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#intransitive" title="Appendix:Glossary">intransitive</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> emerging usage in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_English" class="extiw" title="w:British English">British</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span></span> To watch, or participate, in sexual activity in a public place.

<li><span class="usage-label-sense"><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#intransitive" title="Appendix:Glossary">intransitive</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#transitive" title="Appendix:Glossary">transitive</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span></span> To intentionally restrict one's productivity as employee; to work at the slowest rate that goes unpunished.

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_3">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Etymology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a class="mw-selflink-fragment" href="#English">dog</a></i>. Cognate with <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tok_Pisin" class="extiw" title="w:Tok Pisin">Tok Pisin</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="tpi"><a href="/wiki/dok#Tok_Pisin" title="dok">dok</a></i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pronunciation_3">Pronunciation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Pronunciation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Wiktionary:International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="Wiktionary:International Phonetic Alphabet">IPA</a><sup>(<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bislama_phonology" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Bislama phonology">key</a>)</sup>: <span class="IPA">/ˈdoɡ/</span></li>
<li>Hyphenation: <span class="Latn" lang="bi">dog</span></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_2">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Noun"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<ol><li><a href="#English">dog</a></li></ol>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="References_2">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: References"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Chinese">Chinese</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Chinese"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_1_2">Etymology 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Etymology 1"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a class="mw-selflink-fragment" href="#English">dog</a></i>, which is translation of <i class="Hani mention" lang="zh"><a href="/wiki/%E7%8B%97#Chinese" title="狗">狗</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="zh-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">gau2</span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">dog</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, which is a homophone of <i class="Hani mention" lang="zh"><a href="/wiki/%E4%B9%9D#Chinese" title="九">九</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="zh-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">gau2</span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">nine</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, which is a euphemism of <i class="Hant mention" lang="zh"><a href="/wiki/%E9%B3%A9#Chinese" title="鳩">鳩</a></i><span class="Zsym mention" style="font-size:100%;">／</span><i class="Hans mention" lang="zh"><a href="/wiki/%E9%B8%A0#Chinese" title="鸠">鸠</a></i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span lang="zh-Latn" class="mention-tr tr Latn">gau1</span>, <span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">“</span><span class="mention-gloss">fucking; stupid</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">”</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Danish">Danish</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Danish"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_4">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Etymology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Danish_language" class="extiw" title="w:Old Danish language">Old Danish</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="gmq-oda"><a href="/wiki/dogh#Old_Danish" title="dogh">dogh</a></i>, which was borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Low_German" class="extiw" title="w:Middle Low German">Middle Low German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="gml"><a href="/wiki/doch#Middle_Low_German" title="doch">doch</a></i>, ultimately from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="gem-pro"><a href="/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-Germanic/%C3%BEauh" title="Reconstruction:Proto-Germanic/þauh">*þauh</a></i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adverb">Adverb</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Adverb"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><span class="headword-line"><strong class="Latn headword" lang="da">dog</strong></span>
</p>
<ol><li><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/however#English" title="however">however</a>
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="da">Det er <b>dog</b> ikke sikkert, at de taler sandt.</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">It is, <b>however</b>, not certain that they are telling the truth.</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li>
<li><span class="use-with-mention"><span class="Latn" lang="en">Conveying impressedness, emotional affectation, bewilderment.</span></span>
<dl><dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="da">Hvor er den hund <b>dog</b> nuttet!</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">How cute that dog is!</span></dd></dl></div></dd>
<dd><div class="h-usage-example"><i class="Latn mention e-example" lang="da">Sikke dramatisk du <b>dog</b> kan fremstille sagen!</i><dl><dd><span class="e-translation">How dramatically you can present the matter!</span></dd></dl></div></dd></dl></li></ol>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dutch">Dutch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Dutch"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_5">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Etymology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Borrowed from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a class="mw-selflink-fragment" href="#English">dog</a></i>. Attested since the 16th century.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pronunciation_6">Pronunciation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Pronunciation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Wiktionary:International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="Wiktionary:International Phonetic Alphabet">IPA</a><sup>(<a href="/wiki/Appendix:Dutch_pronunciation" title="Appendix:Dutch pronunciation">key</a>)</sup>: <span class="IPA">/dɔx/</span></li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_5">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Noun"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><span class="headword-line"><strong class="Latn headword" lang="nl">dog</strong>&nbsp;<span class="gender"><abbr title="masculine gender">m</abbr></span> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl p-form-of" lang="nl"><a href="/wiki/doggen#Dutch" title="doggen">doggen</a></b>, <i><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#diminutive" title="Appendix:Glossary">diminutive</a></i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-nl diminutive-form-of" lang="nl"><a href="/wiki/dogje#Dutch" title="dogje">dogje</a></b>&nbsp;<span class="gender"><abbr title="neuter gender">n</abbr></span>)</span>
</p>
<ol><li>A large <span class="Latn" lang="en"><a class="mw-selflink-fragment" href="#English">dog</a></span>, especially one of certain <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/breed#English" title="breed">breeds</a>.</li></ol>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mbabaram">Mbabaram</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Mbabaram"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_8">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=dog&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Etymology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From <i class="Latn mention" lang="vmb"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconstruction:Mbabaram/dwog(a)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Reconstruction:Mbabaram/dwog(a) (page does not exist)">*dwog(a)</a></i>, from <i class="Latn mention" lang="vmb"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconstruction:Mbabaram/udwoga&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Reconstruction:Mbabaram/udwoga (page does not exist)">*udwoga</a></i>, from <i class="Latn mention" lang="vmb"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconstruction:Mbabaram/gudwaga&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Reconstruction:Mbabaram/gudwaga (page does not exist)">*gudwaga</a></i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pama%E2%80%93Nyungan_languages" class="extiw" title="w:Pama–Nyungan languages">Proto-Pama-Nyungan</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="aus-pam-pro"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Reconstruction:Proto-Pama-Nyungan/gudaga&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Reconstruction:Proto-Pama-Nyungan/gudaga (page does not exist)">*gudaga</a></i>. Related to <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dyirbal_language" class="extiw" title="w:Dyirbal language">Dyirbal</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="dbl"><a href="/wiki/guda#Dyirbal" title="guda">guda</a></i>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yidiny_language" class="extiw" title="w:Yidiny language">Yidiny</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="yii"><a href="/wiki/gudaga#Yidiny" title="gudaga">gudaga</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#false_cognate" title="Appendix:Glossary">False cognate</a> of <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language" class="extiw" title="w:English language">English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a class="mw-selflink-fragment" href="#English">dog</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-anderson_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anderson-10">[2]</a></sup>
